Local News Two

Li Jishen's Residence 205

Wireless Radio Stolen

Five Robbers Arrive Suddenly

Forcibly Remove Wireless Radio and Leave

After Investigation, All Five Robbers Arrested

At 2:45 PM yesterday, five robbers first went to the Feilong Car Company at No. 696 Edward Road and rented two cars. They drove to the residence of Li Jishen, an important figure in the National Government, on Luban Road in the French Concession, and stole a wireless radio worth over 7,000 taels. However, within two hours, the case was solved and all five robbers were arrested. The details are as follows:

Young Man Rents Cars: At 2:40 PM yesterday afternoon, a young customer in Western clothes, speaking in a local accent and giving the name Zhang, suddenly arrived at the Feilong Car Company at No. 696 Xixin Bridge on Edward Road. He said he needed to rent two cars until 4:10 PM, stating that the rental fee was 8.60 dollars. The company's cashier then ordered car drivers Xu Bingwen (from Tongzhou) and He Acai (from Changzhou) to drive business car No. 18242 (city No. 4201) and black-plated car No. 8605.

Wireless Radio: After the price was agreed upon, four more people arrived, all dressed in long gowns. They talked to the young man briefly and then all boarded the cars together, driving directly to Luban Road and stopping at the entrance of Lane 163. The five men got out of the cars and walked into Building No. 3. The two drivers waited inside the cars. After about 45 minutes, the five men came out with a large wireless radio and loaded it into the cars. The five men then calmly boarded the cars again and ordered the drivers to drive to Avenue Joffre.

Identifying the Numbers: Building No. 3 is the residence of Li Jishen, an important figure in the National Government. A shortwave wireless radio was installed in the residence, allowing direct communication between Nanjing and Shanghai. Unexpectedly, all five men were robbers, and it is unknown how they suddenly had the idea of posing as police officers to rent cars and steal the radio. At the time, the people in Li's residence were initially unaware of what was happening. Considering that the location was in the Concession and they should have come with Chinese and Western detectives, and seeing that the five men were neither merchants nor students, they suspected their actions. They ordered a servant to chase to the entrance of the lane and identify the two car numbers, and immediately reported to the police station.

Tracking the Robbers: Upon receiving the report, the police station immediately dispatched Chinese Chief Inspector Jin Jiulin, Chief Detective Li Yaolong, Deputy Detectives Zhang Zili and Qian Yuming, and detective Cui Guo, to search in all directions. They also went to the Car Affairs Office to check the two cars, and learned that they had both been rented from Feilong. They urgently went to Feilong to inquire about the situation. According to the drivers, when the cars arrived at Avenue Joffre, they unloaded the radio into a bungalow. The five men then boarded the cars again and drove straight to the New Eastern Hotel at the intersection of Xizang Road and Beihai Road. The young man then paid 8.80 dollars.

Five Criminals Arrested: Upon hearing this, the detectives first drove black-plated car No. 8605 to the police station for temporary detention. They then led all the detectives directly to the New Eastern Hotel to inquire about their appearance and clothing. They arrested six people in room 402 on the fourth floor. Except for one leatherworker who was not involved, the five were all criminals. The mastermind was named Li Zijie. They were all taken to the police station. After a thorough interrogation by the police chief, the location of the stolen goods was traced. They were ordered to be detained separately, awaiting transfer to the court for prosecution.

Disposal of Garbage Issues 206

Various Methods Discussed

Chinese and Concession Authorities Cooperate

According to the Continental Daily, yesterday (the 13th), representatives from the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, Public Works Bureau, and the Engineering Departments of the two concessions, along with the Whangpoo Conservancy Board, met at the Public Works Department to discuss the problem of garbage dumping in the Whangpoo River. After a half-day meeting, various methods were decided upon, some of which will be implemented immediately, such as: (1) Due to the difficulty of supervision at night, garbage boats will be prohibited from operating at night in the future; (2) More supervisors will be stationed in the Whangpoo River to prevent garbage boats from dumping waste along the way; (3) A canal will be dug at the Longhua Mouth garbage storage area to allow garbage boats to enter and unload; (4) Police will be stationed at the garbage storage area to supervise; (5) Garbage boats must be covered to prevent odors from escaping and to prevent dumping along the way; (6) When loading garbage onto boats, it must first be weighed. The manager will fill out a ticket and give it to the boat owner, who will then present it to the manager at the storage area for re-weighing, so that the boat owner will not dare to dump along the way; (7) Boat owners who violate the regulations will be severely punished. The Chief Engineer of the Whangpoo Conservancy Board, Mr. Fessard, has estimated the cost of digging the canal near Longhua Mouth. According to Mr. Fessard, the total cost of the canal is not very high and is within the capabilities of the Shanghai Municipality. The plan is to dig a canal in the middle of the garbage storage area, 300 feet long, 80 feet wide, and 6 feet deep, with embankments on both sides so that covered garbage boats can dock and unload. It is said that during yesterday's meeting, the concession authorities raised the issue of the long-term suitability of the current garbage storage area, fearing that once a proper plan is implemented, the Chinese authorities might suddenly decide that Longhua Mouth is no longer suitable for garbage storage, resulting in wasted effort and expense. However, according to a certain gentleman from the Health Bureau, the Shanghai Municipal Government is very willing to cooperate with the two concession authorities to ensure that the decisions made at yesterday's meeting are fully implemented. Representatives from the two concessions have already contacted the municipal government regarding a five-year lease agreement for the Longhua Mouth storage area. The municipal government is currently considering this matter and is expected to respond within a few days. It is noted that garbage from the northern and southern districts of Shanghai and the two concessions is currently contracted out to laborers who transport it daily to the open space at Longhua Mouth for villagers to purchase as fertilizer. However, the transport boats often seek convenience by dumping waste along the Whangpoo River, causing the waterways to become clogged and the water sources to become polluted. Although the authorities have repeatedly taken measures to stop this practice, they have been largely ineffective. Since the outbreak of the Shanghai War, this practice has become even more prevalent, with an estimated 1,000 tons of garbage being dumped into the Whangpoo River daily. Since the city's drinking water is sourced from the Whangpoo River, polluting the water sources can easily lead to epidemics, which is very harmful to public health. Since the Continental Daily proposed taking measures to stop this practice on the 27th of last month, the authorities have gradually paid more attention, leading to yesterday's meeting. However, while the garbage problem has seen some improvement, the issue of sewage discharge into the waterways, which is also a source of epidemics, also deserves attention from the authorities, so that it can be remedied.

Promoting National Goods While Privately Importing Inferior Goods 207

Gu Zhengfu's Despicable and Clever Scheme

Falsely Printing Trademarks of National Goods Factories

Many Inferior Goods and Fabrics Confiscated

Shop Employees Arrested, Gu Has Fled

Gu Zhengfu, a native of Pudong and owner of the Zhenkang Cloth Store at No. 13 Zunde Lane, Xiamen Road, south of Old Garbage Bridge, specializes in privately selling Japanese goods. Since the beginning of the boycott of Japanese goods, Gu has not only failed to change his ways but has instead increased the quantity of his private sales during this time of national crisis. In addition to selling them privately on an ongoing basis, he stockpiles the remainder in foreign warehouses such as Baohe and Donglai along the northern bank of the Suzhou Creek, waiting for prices to rise. His method of reselling inferior goods is quite clever, which is why he has never been discovered. Gu usually uses the slogan of promoting national goods as a cover. While privately importing inferior goods, he still trades with the Meilun Weaving Factory and the Hongzhang Dyeing Factory, and then privately prints the trademarks of these two factories and pastes them onto the inferior goods and fabrics. After this disguise, and with a slight reduction in prices, people are fooled, blindly follow suit, and recognize these inferior goods as national goods. Now, the secret has been fully uncovered by the Meilun and Hongzhang factories. Considering that Gu's despicable behavior not only undermines the patriotic movement but also damages the reputation of the two factories, they reported the matter to the Old Gate Police Station at 4:00 PM the day before yesterday, requesting a thorough investigation. Detective Tang Si, Su Changsheng, and Detective Liu Junqing, along with Western detectives, rushed to the Zhenkang Cloth Store to search. They found three large boxes of fabrics falsely labeled as national goods, each box containing about 30 to 40 bolts. Gu Zhengfu had already fled upon hearing the news. Only Gu Zhengda, also known as Gu Zhucheng, an employee of the store and a native of Pudong, was arrested. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special District Local Court, where Judge Ge Shixun conducted the preliminary hearing. According to Hu Jiabao, the police station's lawyer, the defendant is being prosecuted under Article 268 of the Criminal Code for obstructing agriculture, industry, and commerce. The lawyer stated that the defendant's counterfeit goods are stored in large quantities in the Baohe and Donglai foreign warehouses, and the police station will search them. Therefore, he requested that the case be adjourned. Subsequently, Xia Sihua, the representative of the Meilun Factory, testified that all the fabrics woven by Meilun are yarn-warp and yarn-weft, while the defendant's counterfeit products are thread-warp and yarn-weft, which is immediately obvious. Furthermore, the representative of the Hongzhang Factory testified that when the fabrics dyed by Hongzhang are burned with fire, the yarn will immediately curl up, while the yarn of inferior goods will remain straight and not shrink after burning. All of these can be tested immediately. The defendant then hired lawyer Lin Yingqing to request bail for release pending trial, but the police station's lawyer immediately stood up to oppose, stating that there is still a lot of evidence waiting to be investigated, and if the defendant is granted bail, there is a risk of him destroying it. Judge Ge then denied the request and ordered the defendant to be detained for trial at a later date.

Do Not Pick Up Broken Electrical Wires 208

A Fisherman Electrocuted and Dies

The electrical wires on Song Park Road in Zhabei were all destroyed by the Japanese army after the war, resulting in broken wires scattered everywhere. The day before yesterday, a fisherman named Jia, about 40 years old, passed through the area and, unaware of the electricity, picked up an electrical wire to help him walk. Unexpectedly, upon touching it, he was immediately electrocuted and fell to the ground, dying on the spot. Since the fisherman had no family, the local leader, Yang Junsheng, reported the incident to the local court for verification.

Standing Director and Deputy Manager 209

Colluding in Fraud

The Yongyu Company Entrusted the Wrong People

Chairman Has Filed a Lawsuit

The Yongyu Heji Textile Co., Ltd., located at No. 3 Jiqing Lane, Jiangxi Road, was established in 1930. In March of last year, the company's board of directors elected Liu Manruo as the Standing Director and hired Gu Ziyan as the Deputy Manager to assist in handling company affairs. In April of this year, the shareholders held a general meeting and decided to hire accountant Xu Guangde to investigate all business accounts. As a result of the audit, it was discovered that Liu and Gu had been colluding in fraud. The methods of fraud included: (1) Fabricating account names and share amounts on the company's blank stock certificates to borrow money from banks, totaling 80,000 taels; (2) Purchasing large quantities of American cotton without initially recording them in the accounts, and only recording them in the company's accounts when losses were incurred, amounting to more than 100,5241 taels; (3) Misappropriating 176,547 taels and 89 cents; and (4) Liu Manruo personally misappropriating 13,271 taels and 95 cents. The company's chairman, Xu Shengchan, hired lawyers Zhang Shijian, Wu Jingxiong, and Yu Chengxiu to file a criminal complaint with the First Special District Local Court against Liu and Gu for embezzling shareholders' funds, engaging in speculation, and misappropriating public funds, requesting that they be summoned and punished under Articles 357 and 366 of the Criminal Code. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu opened the court to hear the case. Both defendants failed to appear in court. According to bailiff Jin Wanyun, Gu lives at No. 1 Yanping Lane, Jing'an Temple Road, and Liu lives at No. 13 Fenjin Lane, Xiahfei Road. Upon summoning them, it was reported that they had both left Shanghai. Therefore, the plaintiff's lawyer requested the issuance of arrest warrants, and Judge Wu ordered the case to be adjourned pending further investigation.

Female Student Missing 210

A Young Woman Impersonates a Relative and Picks Her Up in a Car

Real Family Members Went to Visit, But She Was Gone

Song Xueyi, a native of Wujin, residing at No. 189 Jinde Lane, Route Muro Ming in the Public Concession, has a daughter named Bing Shu, nine years old. In mid-March of this year, she was sent to study at the Chongde Girls' School in Xujiahui and boarded at the school. According to the school's regulations, boarding students are allowed to be visited by family members every Wednesday. Therefore, the Song family sent someone to visit every Wednesday for the past four months, and everything was fine. Unexpectedly, the other day, Song's father, Xueyi, went to visit in person but could not find his daughter. According to Vice Principal Zhou of the school, at 8:00 AM on a certain morning, an unknown young woman arrived at the school in a car, claiming that the student Song Bing Shu's aunt was critically ill and urgently wanted Bing Shu to return home to visit. At that time, the principal saw that the woman was serious and did not suspect anything, so she allowed her to take Bing Shu away. Song Xueyi was shocked and bewildered upon hearing this, as there was no such matter. He immediately sent people to search everywhere, but there was no news. A Murdered Male Corpse Discovered on an Open Space on Yanping Road 211

Resembling a Worker

Suffered Five Knife Wounds

On the open space next to the Kang Nao Tuo Road and Yanping Road in Western Shanghai, yesterday morning at about 6:20 AM, a murdered, unidentified male corpse was discovered. The details are as follows:

Discovery: Yesterday, just as dawn was breaking, on the open space next to Kang Nao Tuo Road (constructed by the Shanghai Municipal Council beyond the boundary) and Yanping Road, next to the Shen Garden dog racing track, Police Chief Li of the Kangjia Bridge Police Station in the Sixth District was on patrol when he noticed a man lying dead on the ground, his head covered in blood. Suspecting that he had been murdered, he immediately reported it to the District Chief.

Murder Scene: After receiving the report, District Chief Zhang of the Sixth District instructed Inspector Xu to conduct a thorough investigation. It was found that the murdered, unidentified male corpse was about 30 years old, wearing a blue cloth jacket, a black small cloth shirt underneath, black cloth trousers, straight woolen shoes, and had a shaved head, resembling a worker. His neck was tightly wrapped with a hemp rope. There were two forceful wounds on the top of his head, two on the back of his head, and one on the side of his face, totaling five knife wounds. A sharp blade was found on the ground next to the corpse. It is believed that the murderer strangled him with a hemp rope and then stabbed him to death with a sharp blade.

Request for Examination: District Chief Zhang, considering that the matter was a murder case, immediately instructed local leader Shen Jinlin to report it to the local court, requesting that personnel be sent to examine it. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Yang was dispatched by the court, along with an examiner, to examine the scene. It was determined that the unidentified male corpse had indeed been strangled and stabbed to death. There were rope marks on his neck, and a total of five knife wounds on his head. As the corpse's relatives could not be found, the local leader was instructed to report to the hall to prepare a coffin and collect the corpse. It is also reported that the relevant police station also sent officers to examine the scene and take a photograph.

Post Office Hours Resume Yesterday 212

Returning to the State Before January 28th

The office hours of the Shanghai Post Office were shortened after the outbreak of the Shanghai Incident. Later, as our army withdrew its defenses, the hours were gradually extended. Now that the war has long ended and everything has returned to normal, Chief Postmaster General Zaplin specially instructed all department staff to resume office hours as before January 28th. The instruction reads: "Regarding the matter of instructions, the working hours of all employees have been repeatedly revised. They have been ordered to comply with Bureau Instructions No. 790, 1794, and 1797, which have been issued successively. It is hereby decided that, starting from the 14th of this month, all offices should uniformly operate according to the hours stipulated before January 28th to emphasize postal services. You are all to comply with this order." Chief Postmaster General Zaplin.

Sauce and Liquor Industry 213

Requests Exemption from Liquor Tax in Hongkou District

Public Works Department Responds Vaguely

Decision to Continue the Struggle

The Sauce and Liquor Trade Association, previously due to members such as Fulai in the Hongkou District jointly submitting a letter to the association, requesting that it forward a letter to the Public Works Department requesting exemption from liquor tax for one quarter due to the war period, forwarded the request with the circumstances. The association has now received a reply from the Public Works Department, stating that a list of all numbers eligible for tax exemption must be submitted for review. The wording is vague and there is still no satisfactory answer. The association specially convened a meeting of sauce and liquor merchants in the Hongkou District at the Liquor Trade Association in the city to discuss the matter. Over 200 people attended. According to the report, dozens of companies, including Sheng Taifeng, Yi Kang, and Lao Fulai, have already been exempted from liquor tax for two months. Many have paid liquor tax for the entire spring and summer seasons, and it should be considered how to remedy this. After discussion, it was decided to continue the struggle. The points of request are as follows: (1) Base the liquor tax exemption standard on the patrol and concession exemption area; (2) Those who have paid the full liquor tax for the spring and summer seasons should be deducted from the autumn liquor tax; (3) When filling out the autumn liquor tax tickets, the amount of exemption should be deducted to avoid disputes when collecting the tax; (4) The form for filling out the exemption should be easily filled out by the sauce and liquor merchants and submitted to the Chinese Taxpayer Association for transfer to the Public Works Department for approval.

Robbery in Renmei Lane Yesterday Morning 214

At 9:30 yesterday morning, six or seven well-dressed robbers suddenly arrived at No. 3, West Lane, Renmei Lane, West Xinqiao Street, French Concession. Under the pretext of searching for opium, two of the robbers, armed with pistols, first drove all the people upstairs downstairs and locked them in the east side room, then went upstairs to rob. After about an hour, they each escaped with their stolen goods. The widow surnamed Zhang in the living room upstairs suffered the most losses, with jewelry and cash totaling about 1,000 yuan. The Luo family in the east wing lost more than 100 yuan. The second landlord, surnamed Bian, was not affected because no one was at home. The luckiest was the reporter who rented the front east wing room downstairs, who was not visited. Afterwards, the victims reported the situation to the police station, requesting a pursuit.

Robbers Attempt to Steal a Boatload of Foreign Yarn 217

They Waited Too Long for the Tugboat and Fled

Two Crew Members Shot by Robbers

Cao Ahe, a local, owned a small vessel. The other day, he loaded 100 bales of yarn for a certain company and moored it overnight at the Sima Road pier. Unexpectedly, at 12:00 PM, eight robbers, each armed with a gun, jumped onto the boat, tied up the crew members in a corner, and forbade them from making any noise. When Gu Haifu, a crew member from Chongming, shouted loudly, he was shot in the arm by the robbers with a Mauser pistol. The bullet did not penetrate, and Gu was injured and fell on the boat. Cai Dalang, also from Chongming, was also severely injured by the robbers with an iron rod. However, the robbers were very ambitious. Their goal was to use a small tugboat to tow the entire boatload of yarn away and sell it, but the hired tugboat did not arrive after a long wait. Fearing that waiting too long would cause them to be discovered by the police, the robbers went ashore and fled. Gu Haifu, who was shot with a Mauser bullet, was able to go to Renji Hospital for treatment, and it is said that the bullet has been removed. After this case occurred, the Customs Water Police Station sent four detectives, Nos. 19, 73, 36, and 40, to the empty dock on Sima Road. A suspect, Huang Fuqiang, 30 years old, from Chongming, was captured and immediately taken into custody for interrogation.

Bomb Explosion, Four Dead and Two Injured 219

Three Dye Workers and an Old Woman Die Tragically

Next to the Qingyun Bridge on Qingyun Road in Zhabei, opposite the World Grand Theater, there is an open space of about three acres with green grass and bamboo fences, which has always been the drying yard of the Jiuda Dyeing Factory at No. 693 Tiantong'an Road. Yesterday (the 14th), at about 10:00 AM, four dye workers from the factory, including Pan A Chao, were resting on the lawn after finishing work in the yard and took out the pre-brought playing cards to play. While they were in high spirits, two Jiangbei scavenger children were digging for garbage under the bamboo fence along Qingyun Road in the yard when they suddenly touched a wire. A loud explosion suddenly occurred in the yard. The two children knew they had caused trouble and ran away in terror. However, the four dye workers sitting in the yard were caught off guard and unable to escape. As a result, two workers, Wang Bingcai and He Aqing, were wounded by the bomb and were in critical condition. The other two, Pan A Chao and Xu Jinquan, died on the spot. When the bomb exploded, the shrapnel flew out more than 30 feet, reached the overhanging building at the entrance of Tianshou Lane to the north of the yard, blasting a hole, shattering the glass windows. When the shrapnel landed, it pierced the chest and back of a Changshu old woman who was standing idly at the entrance of the alley, residing at No. 1 of the lane, in Xu Rongxing's clothing store, killing her instantly. It is said that the old woman was 66 years old. She had taken refuge elsewhere during the war and had only returned for less than a month before suddenly dying tragically. After the incident, the Jiuda Dyeing Factory reported to the Public Security Bureau's Fifth District Office and the local court to inspect the scene. Three injured workers, Wang Binglin, Shen Changqing, and He Zhiqing, were all sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment. However, Wang Binglin's legs were blown off and he was severely injured. He arrived at the hospital at about 10:00 AM and died of his injuries at 2:30 PM. Shen Changqing was injured in his right leg, and He Zhiqing was wounded in his leg and waist. The injuries were quite severe. All of the injured were from Shaoxing.

Four Banks Issue Preparation Report 223

128th Time

The Four Banks Reserve Vault is jointly established by the Salt Industry Bank, Jin City Bank, Zhongnan Bank, and Continental Bank, specializing in the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the vault's issuance regulations, banknotes are issued with full reserves. Cash reserves must be at least 60%, and guarantee reserves must be at most 40%. An announcement is made every week, and it is checked by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. The Shanghai Reserve Vault's 128th announcement on June 11, 1932, is recorded as follows: Amount of banknotes in circulation: 18,486,357 yuan; Total amount of reserves: 18,486,357 yuan; including: Cash reserves: 11,355,014 yuan and 87 cents; Guarantee reserves: 7,131,342 yuan and 12 cents.

First Special Court 224

Clearing Accumulated Cases in War Zones

Dispatching the Head of the First Criminal Court to be Responsible for Clearing

Since the January 28th Incident, the Shanghai First Special District Local Court has been close to the war zone. Therefore, the litigants often feared being caught in the crossfire when the court date arrived, and could not appear in court to respond to the lawsuit. After the end of the war, due to the relocation of addresses, most could not be reached. Although President Zhou Xianjue issued a notice, urging the litigants to report their addresses within a certain period and await summons, this series of twists and turns resulted in a mountain of civil lawsuits in the court. Now that the situation in society has completely recovered, President Zhou has decided to actively clear the accumulated cases in the shortest possible time, so as not to burden the people for too long with lawsuits. He has appointed Zhou Han, the head of the First Criminal Court, to be solely responsible for clearing the accumulated civil cases from this month. After being entrusted, Judge Zhou immediately consulted with Li Hu, the head of the Civil Court, and immediately began to receive the cases accumulated during the war, arranging the order of trial, so as to expedite the trial and end it as soon as possible. As for the duties of the First Criminal Court, which rotate three days a week on Tuesdays, Thursdays, and Saturdays, President Zhou has separately appointed criminal judges Feng Shide and Shen Bingrong to take turns as acting judges. All have reported for duty.

All Iron Wire Fences in the Concession Removed 225

Since the outbreak of the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, the Public Concession Police Department had erected iron wire fences in various areas at the junction of the Chinese area and the concession, blocking pedestrians from entering and exiting. After the conclusion of the ceasefire agreement, all but the intersection of the North Railway Station Baoshan Road and the concession road had been gradually removed and traffic restored. Yesterday, the authorities of the above mentioned location, the Huisi Police Station, ordered Chinese workers to dismantle the fences entirely.

Trademark Bureau Urges All Industries to Register 226

He Zhuoxian, Director of the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, yesterday sent letters to various trade associations, stating that Chinese merchants have often disregarded trademark rights and interests, resulting in countless cases of trademark infringement by others due to unregistered trademarks, causing business losses. The Bureau is in charge of trademark administration and believes that trademark registration is of great importance to the development of commerce and the interests of merchants. Universal registration is the only way to fulfill the intention of the state in establishing a specialized bureau. Many of your members have already been using trademarks but have not applied for registration. The hope is that your association will assist in the investigation, widely publicize this information, and instruct those with unregistered trademarks to register with the Bureau immediately. These procedures are extremely simple. If there is any unclear point, please introduce them to the Bureau at any time to inquire about everything. This concerns the interests of merchants, and assistance with publicity is highly appreciated.

Record of the Shareholders' Meeting of Daxing Vegetable Market 231

Additional Shares of 10,000 Yuan Raised

The Daxing Vegetable Market, built at the intersection of Zhongxing Road and Datong Road in Zhabei, was originally scheduled to open on February 1st of this year. Unexpectedly, on the evening of January 28th, the war suddenly broke out, leading to its suspension. Later, the vegetable market was bombed by Japanese projectiles, causing heavy losses. Although it has now been repaired and completed, the original share capital of 30,000 yuan has already been used up. The current repair costs are all borrowed by the general manager, Yang Dexin, from various places. Therefore, at about 2 p.m. yesterday, all the shareholders were specially convened to hold a meeting to discuss the matter. As a result, it was resolved that each share of the original 20 shares of regular shares, each worth 1,500 yuan, totaling 30,000 yuan, would increase by one additional share each, each share being set at 500 yuan, totaling 10,000 yuan, to offset the losses and repair costs of this war. At that time, there were already four shares that had been subscribed. The rest must be paid successively. Finally, it was decided that the official opening would be on July 1st. Unless there are unexpected changes, there will be no postponement.

Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Trials Clerical Trainees 234

In order to improve office convenience, the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities intends to recruit five child laborers, specializing in errands in the office, providing them with remedial education and practical experience. In the future, they can be promoted to staff, so they are called clerical trainees. Their position is between the servant and the staff. Their qualifications are: (1) Between 16 and 18 years old; (2) Healthy body, passing the doctor's examination; (3) Elementary school level, passing the examination; (4) Neat appearance, agile nature; (5) Qualified with a reliable guarantee. They will be tested for a few months, and given a monthly wage of eight yuan, in addition to providing accommodation and uniforms. If they are satisfied with the completion of the period, they will be officially hired, and the monthly wage will be increased to ten yuan. Thereafter, it can be increased by two or four yuan every year. If there are those who wish to apply, they can go to the General Affairs Section of the First Department of the Bureau on the west end of the Municipal Government Road from June 16th to the 25th, every Friday, Saturday, and Sunday from 9 a.m. to 11 a.m. to read the regulations, register for the examination. If qualified, they will be notified to come to the Bureau on July 1st, otherwise no reply will be given.

Elementary School Teacher 236

Falsely Claiming to be a Anti-Drug Association Investigator

Searching for Opium and Extorting Huge Sums of Money

The Victim Who Smokes is Also Convicted

Ni Jie, a native of Haimen who claims to be a teacher at Peizheng School, lives at No. 19 Huaxingfang, Yangshupu Road. At around 6 p.m. the day before yesterday, together with Shi Lifeng, a teacher at the same school, he posed as an investigator of the Anti-Drug Association, carrying a forged official document from Zhong Ketuo, the deputy director of the Anti-Drug Association, and a submission from Lu Yaoming, a reporter. They suddenly went to the home of Tang Youguang (also known as Tang Biekai), a resident of No. 16 Shouchun Lane, Metthurst Road, claiming to be ordered to come and search for opium. When they saw a set of opium lamps and guns and half a tael of opium paste on the bed, they pointed out that he was selling it and threatened to extort 2,000 yuan. Tang's wife secretly went out and secretly reported to two Chinese detectives at No. 297 and No. 999, saying that there was a robbery alarm in her house. The detectives rushed to the scene, but Ni and others had already escaped after hearing the news. Ni Jie was arrested on the spot, while Shi Lifeng escaped. The detectives then entered the room and took Tang Youguang and the opium paraphernalia to the Gordon Road Police Station. The police chief ordered them to be detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. According to Wang Yaotang, the police station's lawyer, Ni Jie is now accused of attempted extortion under Article 370 of the Criminal Code, and Tang Youguang is accused of illegally possessing opium paraphernalia and smoking opium under Article 11 of the Anti-Opium Law. The above circumstances were described in detail, and two forged official documents were presented to the court for investigation. When questioned, Ni Jie confessed that the official document was delivered by Yang Shouren, Tang's brother-in-law. Yesterday, he went to Tang's house with Yang and Shi, and Yang and Shi talked with Tang, but he did not open his mouth. Regarding the extortion of 2,000 yuan, he claimed that he did not know about it. Tang hired a lawyer to appear in court to defend him and admitted to smoking opium. Judge Wu Tingqi verified the confession and sentenced Ni Jie to three months of imprisonment for conspiracy to forge documents and attempted extortion. The forged instructions and submissions were confiscated. Tang was sentenced to one month of imprisonment and fined 200 yuan. The opium paraphernalia were confiscated.

Li Bixia Accuses Weng and Husband 238

Demanding Alimony of 30,000 Yuan

Wu Zhenxiang, the son of Wu Tingfan, manager of Yongju Bank in Ningbo Road, remarried Li Bixia, the elder sister of Li Yumen, an employee of the Bank of Communications, after being divorced in 1925. They married in their hometown of Zhenhai. At that time, the bride was still young. Soon, Wu took his beloved wife to Shanghai, and they separated from the big family and lived in No. 107 Zixia Road, Nanshi, enjoying the sweet life of a husband and wife. It was appropriate to enjoy the joy of harmony, but for several years, there has been little harmony and much discord. Now, they are involved in a public lawsuit. Li is accusing her husband and father-in-law of neglecting alimony, and is asking the court to order the two defendants to pay alimony of 30,000 yuan. The Wu father and son, being accused, hired lawyer Wang Peiyuan to file a plea, stating that the plaintiff had been disrespectful to elders and had beaten the children born to the previous wife after she married into the family. After persuasion by relatives and friends, she separated from her relatives, hoping that she would repent. However, shortly after moving, she relapsed and beat the children, causing public outrage among the neighbors. The landlord refused to renew the lease. She moved to Shanghai in February last year. However, she became obsessed with the glamour of Shanghai and spent money extravagantly. The defendant suffered a terrible business failure and was worried about the plaintiff's unreasonable troubles. As a result of resentment, he became ill and returned to his hometown in November last year to recuperate, as advised by the doctor. The plaintiff was unwilling to return with him and was given a monthly living allowance of 30 yuan. The plaintiff took advantage of the defendant's return to his hometown and moved all the furniture and clothes from the Shanghai residence, which was the same as when she forcibly withdrew 2,000 yuan of deposits and jewelry from her predecessor's Ningbo Yuanchun and other banks. When the defendant returned to Shanghai in April, the plaintiff avoided meeting him and fabricated facts, falsely accusing him of abuse and abandonment, and openly published it in the newspaper, which was obviously for another purpose. After receiving the complaint sent by Junyuan to solve the problem, I learned that she was demanding 30,000 yuan on the basis of false words. When the defendant heard about it, his old illness became worse.

This kind of unreasonable request is not credible in law or emotion, and so on. Yesterday morning, Judge Li summoned the plaintiff and her lawyer He Yiyun to court and stated that she was now unable to pay the litigation fees due to poverty and requested litigation relief. The defendant's lawyer, Wang Peiyuan, objected, saying that the plaintiff had the money to publish in the newspaper, and that her clothing today was not like that of a poor person and did not meet the conditions for relief. Judge Li said that the plaintiff's request for litigation relief would be verified later and approved. As for the claim for clothing and other items, she was ordered to provide a list within three days to await interrogation.

Two Opium Cases in the French Concession 242

The Chinese and Western detectives of the Mailan Police Station in the French Concession learned the day before yesterday that Tongtaihao at No. 3 Zhonghuali, Zhengjia Muqiao Street, was secretly selling opium for profit, which is a clear violation of the prohibition. They immediately rushed to search the place and found Jiang Fuyuan packing opium in the Tingzijian room, while the owner, Tan Chushan, was sitting beside him monitoring. They were arrested together. Six pounds of opium, a balance, a small wooden box, a large pair of scissors, ten yuan of opium money, and six double-corner coins were found under the floor and in the pavilion. They were taken to the police station. The police chief found that Tan had also been arrested and punished twice for privately selling opium. He ordered him to be detained. First, Gu Shouxu, the police station's lawyer, stated the case and sued according to Article 6 of the Anti-Opium Law. Bao Tan Bian Zhixiang also reported the process of searching and arresting the defendants, and presented the opium evidence to the court. Tan confessed that he used to do opium business, but has now stopped. The soil found in the search was left over from before and he did not dare to sell it. Jiang confessed that he was an apprentice and was only in charge of packing and entertaining friends. He also hired a lawyer to defend him. The court verified the confession and announced that Tan Chushan was sentenced to six months of imprisonment and fined 700 yuan for selling opium. Jiang Fuyuan was sentenced to three months of imprisonment and fined 300 yuan. If the fines are converted to imprisonment, they will be calculated at three yuan per day. The number of days of detention before the judgment is determined will be offset against the imprisonment for one day for every two days. The opium found in the search will be confiscated. At the same time, the Chinese and Western detectives of the police station learned that Yuanyuhaho at No. 5 Zhonghuali was also selling opium privately. They went to search the place, but there was no evidence. When the detectives were about to return to the police station, Liu Fanggui happened to bring a small bag of opium to the store and wanted to return the cash. He was stopped by the detectives and questioned. Zhang Zixian, the accountant of the store, and Zhang Senfa, the apprentice, were speechless and had no words to answer. The detectives took them to the police station. Yesterday, they were sent to the Second Criminal Court of the Second Special District. The police station's lawyer, Fei Xizhen, stated the case. Zhang Zixian and Zhang Linfa confessed that they used to do opium business, but have now stopped. The rest of their words were evasive. Liu Fanggui confessed that she had asked a friend to buy it from Yuanyuhaho a month ago because her mother was sick, but she did not smoke it, so she brought it to return it. Judge Wu verified the confession and ordered that the case be heard again at a later date. The defendants were sent back to custody.

Letters to the Editor

The Economic Crisis in China 246

By Mu Xiangyue

The economic crisis in China is not something that started today, but it is at its worst now. The reasons are very complicated, and the biggest reason lies in the economic aggression of the imperialist powers. Economic aggression is different from political aggression. Political aggression uses force.

For example, the violent Japanese aggression in Northeast China and the attack on Shanghai were of great harm, but it was obvious and could make the people of the whole country feel heartbroken and vow never to forget. Economic aggression is different. It replaces military warfare with commercial warfare. Imperialist powers, with the advantage of advanced industrial countries, use machine production to suppress our manual production. Their power penetrates deeply into our inland areas. Even remote and desolate places are filled with foreign goods. That is, there is the power of imperialist powers everywhere, absorbing our money invisibly to control our fate. Over the years, it has made our country's economy increasingly bankrupt, and even though our people suffer, they still do not know why. Political aggression is like an acute infectious disease, which can still be resisted significantly with epidemic prevention methods. Economic

aggression is like chronic tuberculosis, which makes people gradually lose weight and die without realizing it. Therefore, the economic crisis in our country today did not come in a day or two. The outflow of rights and interests has been going on for decades. However, it is only today that the symptoms have gradually become apparent and the economic pain has deepened day by day. Looking forward, it is truly chilling. Now, in order to awaken the people of the country, based on customs reports and the current economic panic, it is used as factual proof.

Since the first year of the Republic of China, the number of foreign goods imported through customs has exceeded the number of local goods exported every year. From the first year to the twentieth year, the least was in the eighth year of the Republic of China, when imports exceeded exports by more than 16 million taels. The most was in the twentieth year, when imports exceeded exports by more than 55.9 million taels. In total, in the 20 years, imports exceeded exports by more than 391.2 million customs taels, equivalent to more than 435.8 million taels of Shanghai silver, and more than 600 billion yuan in national currency at the current market price. May I ask, in a short period of 20 years, because the people of the country like to use foreign goods, making the outflow of money reach more than 600 billion yuan, how can our country not be poor, and how can the national economic situation not experience panic? Not only that, but if the people of our country can understand the cause of poverty, which is due to the excessive outflow of money, and urgently rise up to work hard to produce and promote domestic goods, then the disease can still be cured. Unfortunately, economic panic is still economic panic, and those who like to use foreign goods still like to use foreign goods. According to customs reports, in the three months of this spring, imported foreign goods were 26,100

More than 10,000 taels, and exported local goods were more than 14,100,000 taels. Imports exceeded exports by more than 12,100,000 taels. Not only that, even in Shanghai alone, imports exceeded exports by more than 52,200,000 taels in January, more than 14,400,000 taels in February, and more than 26,600,000 taels in March. In Shanghai alone, in three months, imports exceeded exports by more than 93,300,000 taels. According to Western newspapers, in April, imports in Shanghai alone were more than 54,400,000 taels, and exports were more than 9,900,000 taels. Imports exceeded exports by more than 44,400,000 taels. Therefore, in Shanghai alone, in the four months of this year, imports exceeded exports by more than 138,800,000 taels, equivalent to more than 200 million yuan in national currency. If we consider the whole country, it is at least more than 166 million taels, equivalent to more than 260 million yuan in national currency. This year, when the country is in trouble, in just four months, imports exceeded exports by more than 260 million yuan. The future is boundless, and I really don't know how to continue. The above is only from the perspective of numbers. The economic danger in China is already obvious. Now, let's examine the types of imported goods in the customs report.

In the twentieth year of the Republic of China, the total value of imported goods was more than 130.9 million taels. Among them, cotton goods were more than 14.9 million taels, cotton was more than 13.2 million taels, rice was more than 12.1 million taels, sugar was more than 8.6 million taels, tobacco leaves and cigarettes were more than 5.6 million taels, flour was more than 3.1 million taels, seafood was more than 2.5 million taels, wool fabrics were more than 2.4 million taels, fruits, medicinal materials, etc. were more than 2.3 million taels, timber was more than 2.3 million taels, rayon was more than 1.4 million taels, wheat was more than 1.2 million taels, and canned food was more than 1.2 million taels. These are all necessities for people's lives and all rely on foreign goods. Not only is the outflow of money fearful, but in case of war in the world, traffic is blocked, and foreign goods cannot be imported or imports are reduced, will the people of our country face the danger of lack of supply or interruption of supply of food and clothing? As for machinery, the tools of production, the quantity imported in the same year was only worth more than 4.4 million taels, accounting for only 3.38% of the total import amount of more than 130.9 million taels. It can be seen that more than 90% of imported foreign goods are consumables. Year after year, consumption after consumption, poverty will inevitably become more and more serious. This is what the people of our country must realize.

The symptoms of China's economic illness have gradually become apparent. Domestic finance is becoming increasingly depleted. Exported goods are decreasing day by day, and imported goods are increasing day by day, making domestic cash concentrated in Shanghai. Because cash is concentrated in Shanghai, Shanghai has a surplus of cash, the foreign interest rate shrinks, and the silver exchange rate is low, with no use at all. However, the provinces in the interior, due to financial depletion, lack cash to purchase Shanghai drafts, resulting in soaring prices of Shanghai drafts. Recently, in Jiangxi, because imported foreign goods all come from Shanghai, they have to purchase Shanghai drafts to cope with the situation. At the same time, because too few local goods are exported, there is no money to offset them, resulting in soaring exchange rates. In Jiangxi, purchasing 1,000 taels of Shanghai drafts requires 1,438 yuan in national currency, which is more than 50 yuan higher than usual. As a result, not only has the price of foreign goods in the interior increased by more than 5%, but also local goods from other provinces that are transported to Jiangxi via Shanghai are greatly affected by the high exchange rates. This is just an example. In fact, economic panic is everywhere. It is not just Jiangxi. The main reason is that in the provinces in the interior, soldiers and bandits are fighting, taxes and levies are heavy, transportation is inconvenient, and freight rates are high, resulting in local goods not being able to be exported, or not easily exported. Farmers and workers have no profit to gain, their livelihoods are becoming increasingly difficult, and production is decreasing day by day, resulting in the need to rely on foreign goods for their lives, and domestic finance is thus in dire straits, almost beyond salvation. China has always been known as an agricultural country. Today, rice, wheat, cotton, timber, and tobacco leaves are all major imports of agricultural products. Among them, the import quantity of cotton cloth is the largest. Therefore, today, all of us in the country must concentrate our efforts. Therefore, today, all of us in the country must concentrate our efforts and vigorously implement three things. First, remove production obstacles and work hard to increase production. Second, manage foreign trade and control the import of foreign goods. Third, awaken national thought and work hard to promote domestic goods. All these three things are related. If we can work together and implement them practically, then the economic crisis in China will not become deeper and deeper, and we will have a day to get out of danger and ascend to a prosperous road. This is what I sincerely pray for.

Free Talk

Excerpts from the words of Ma Xiangbo, a nonagenarian

Reading Less Can Reduce Pain 247

— Plum Blossom

My life is both laughable and painful. On one hand, I see foreign science developing day by day, and on the other hand, I see everything in China declining day by day. All I have seen in my life are these contradictory phenomena, how painful! If I could read less, especially less foreign books, I could reduce some pain. But now, everything I see is desolate, and everything I hear is alarming! China's decline, from the Boxers to the Party-State, gets worse with each passing day. Foreign countries are progressing day by day, not only in science but also in politics. For example, all countries used to be monarchies, but now almost all have become democracies. Even countries that maintain a monarchy have become constitutional monarchies. The British monarch has always been a fake emperor. Belgium, a small country, has also had a hereditary fake emperor since 1830. It's funny to say, most of the European emperors were invited from other countries. For example, the Belgian monarch was requested from Germany, and the Bourbon royal family of France was not French themselves. In short, the European concept of emperor is completely different from the Chinese. Therefore, Europeans have the idea of colonialism.

We Chinese are different. We have always had the idea that "there can be only one master in the sky and one king on earth." Therefore, we close ourselves off and have absolutely no idea of colonialism. In fact, when it comes to the sovereignty of politics, neither family rule nor public rule is a thorough way of saying it. To get to the bottom of the matter, sovereignty belongs neither to one person nor to everyone, but to the Creator. In the face of the Creator, all human beings are equal. Therefore, sovereignty belongs to the Creator, and therefore it belongs to everyone. (Editor's note: Old Man Xiang has a firm belief in religion. He advocates democracy, but his theory of democracy is based on religion. It can be said to be a theocratic theory of democracy. It is recorded here for the reference of those who study political theory.)

Sovereignty belongs to the Creator and to everyone. But anyone can fill the main body. For example, the spirit tablet has a soul, but the spirit tablet can be made of any wood. The Japanese worship the Emperor, but the Emperor has no power. This is spirit tablet-ism. The Chinese worship the dead as emperors. This is an innovation of the Party-State, which is far less good than spirit tablet-ism.

Great Calamity Without Fruit 248

— Yu Jianhua

When did the art of character divination begin? It is also called character splitting and breaking characters. It existed before the Sui and Tang Dynasties. The key is to seize the opportunity. Sometimes, it is unknowable. When the Patriotic Women's School moved to Chen Garden on Jiangwan Road, Mr. Sun, who was in charge, worked very hard beforehand. Because several schools were competing for rent at the same time, it would be gone if he was a little slow. One day, Mr. Sun was on his way to Chen Garden. He was compelled by curiosity and tried a character at the door of "Little Confusion." It was the character "奮" (fèn, strive). He privately thought that he must strive to succeed. "Little Confusion" picked up a pen and split the character. The top part was "大" (dà, big), and the middle part was "佳" (jiā, good). He thought it was great. But then he combined it with "凶" (xiōng, ominous) to form "難" (nán, difficult). The bottom part was "田" (tián, field), which was a fruit without wood. So he judged it as "great calamity without fruit." Mr. Sun was still unconvinced and tried another character, "縱" (zòng, vertical, indulge). It was split as follows: the left side was "亂絲" (luàn sī, messy silk), and the top and middle parts were both "人" (rén, person). The right side was "疋" (pǐ, bolt of cloth) that could not become "走" (zǒu, walk). So he said that it was "walking vertically and horizontally without a way out." Mr. Sun was not deeply convinced and dismissed it with a smile. Later, the school's progress was very smooth. Within a year, classrooms were opened, assembly halls were added, and the school's affairs were thriving. He thought that "Little Confusion" was truly confused. Unexpectedly, the January 28th Incident occurred. The school happened to be in the war zone, and most of the school buildings were destroyed. Countless efforts were reduced to ashes. After many difficulties, he was able to find another school site and temporarily start classes. Then, he realized that the so-called "great calamity" was the great calamity of the country, and the "without fruit" meant being destroyed by the Japanese invaders. A year of operation yielded no results. Because it was in the war zone, it still could not operate normally. Therefore, it was said that "walking was impossible." Recently, when Mr. Sun talks about the school's affairs, he smiles and tells people about "great calamity without fruit." I am not a superstitious person, but I record this because it is quite enough to provide conversation.

World Snippets 249

— Sea Guest

A Russian man worked as a cargo unloader at the Corsica station. One night, he suddenly stole a train engine and drove away at full speed. A patrol officer saw him and chased him on foot for three miles along the track. The engine suddenly encountered an obstacle and was finally intercepted. According to the Russian man, he had important business to attend to in a neighboring town and had no choice but to do so.

A British university professor is doing archaeological work. According to his research, the modern beauty pageant originated 450 years before the birth of Christ. It was held regularly in Byzantium, which is now Istanbul, the capital of Turkey. At that time, only women from royal and aristocratic families could participate. The victorious beauties were honored with grand banquets and received enthusiastic celebrations. As for those who unfortunately failed, they could only enter a monastery and become nuns.

The Eiffel Tower in Paris, the capital of France, is 985 feet high and is world-famous. It has not been painted for seven years and has inevitably become dull. Recently, it was repainted. It requires 45 tons of paint.

Overseas Whaling Movement 250

— Laborer

The whale is the largest of the fish species. Overseas, whaling is regarded as one of the major industries. Its value is estimated at approximately US$500 to US$10,000 per tail. In recent years, whaling factories in countries such as the United Kingdom, the United States, and Norway have sprung up. The Norwegian whaling industry is particularly dominant in the world. Therefore, it is also striving for excellence in whaling methods. The June issue of a science magazine has a detailed record, which is excerpted and translated as follows.

In the past, whaling mainly used harpoons. However, whales rely on their huge size and strong resistance, and they are easily missed. It has now been abandoned and completely replaced with ammunition bombing. The method is to suspend bombs on the tips of iron rods and connect them with extremely thick leather wires. If the target is found, the mechanism is immediately activated for bombing. Whales rarely escape when they encounter it. At the same time, mobile factories are organized on ships, patrolling the sea day and night. The best performers can catch six to eight whales per ship per day. The largest whale can yield 75 boxes of oil, each box worth US$26, which can be made into 10,000 squares of high-quality soap. The bones are kept for making toothbrushes and umbrella handles. In order to prevent the extinction of whales, the Norwegian government recently passed a ban in the State Council to preserve whale seeds. Whales that are too small must not be captured. Female whales are absolutely forbidden to be slaughtered.

A Record of the Tomb of Li Zhen, Duke of Cao 251

— Xie Fei

The Chinese Construction Society, organized by Mr. Zhu Qiqian, has elaborated on national studies and ancient architecture. Last year, it accidentally discovered 56 kinds of cultural relics of the Li family of Prince Qiyang. The ink marks are as new as before, and the ancient colors are brilliant. Recently, they were exhibited in the Central Park of Beiping. For a time, newspapers in the north and south were filled with reports. This article also records the beginning and end of the exhibition. I am a descendant of Prince Qiyang. Thinking of the merits of my ancestors and the longevity of my family, I can deeply think of Kang Le and feel the earnest attention of the people of the country. Recently, I received a letter from my family in Mingguang, stating that Yun Cheng and Lu Ping, my two great-uncles, will go to the old capital in North Beiping in about ten days to clarify the cultural relics stored on the ground and combine them with Beiping to make a complete whole. I dare not seek the happiness of one family, but also hope to help the national history.

Li Zhen, Duke of Cao, whose given name is Zhen, is the first ancestor of our Li family. His first wife was Princess Xiaoxin Cao of the Ming Dynasty, the elder sister of Emperor Taizu of the Ming Dynasty. He was buried in Mingguang, about one mile southeast of the city, formerly known as the Village of Miracles. The naming of Mingguang was because Zhu Yuanzhang, Emperor Taizu of the Ming Dynasty, was born there, and there was a purple light shrouded around it. Today, the so-called Diaper Beach, Erlang Temple, Moshan, and Xianghua Temple all have miracles. The joint tomb of the Duke and the Princess is about three feet high and rises like a small hill. There is a

On Frugality and Thrift to Save the Nation (12) 252

— Recounted by Nie Zengjifen, Written by Nan Guijie

There are many books on people's livelihood and social economy. The British are better at it than our ancient philosophers. There are many college students who eat it, but few who use it. Those who do it are quick, and those who use it are comfortable. It is an immutable principle for all ages. Those who eat it but do not produce, specialize in trickery and plunder, and are the parasites of society. They are the so-called parasites that absorb surplus value. Those who use it comfortably refer to all luxury consumer goods. That is, as the Book of Documents says, "Do not do what is useless, harm what is useful, and the work will be accomplished. Do not value foreign objects, devalue useful objects, and the people will be prosperous." There are many other similar words in the Analects, Mencius, the Book of Documents, and the Book of Rites, which can all illuminate each other. Politics cannot be separated from social economy to establish a theory. Recently, people like Adam Smith and Karl Marx, although their words are detailed, their essence cannot add anything to our country's ancient philosophy. Then we know that the intelligence of our ancestors is unattainable. Once the principles of political economy are established, their establishment of education must also be based on these principles. Otherwise, the purpose of political economy cannot be achieved. Self-restraint is the principle of establishing education. Building railways is like knowing how to make trains. Ancient Chinese philosophers also knew the necessity of laying railway tracks. Because without tracks, even if the engine power is sufficient to pull the train, it will inevitably overturn. Now, many Western countries know the theory of social economy. However, if they do not understand the foundation of establishing education, they cannot fully promote its effectiveness. For example, the economic policy of Soviet Russia seems to be close to the advocacy of Confucius and Mencius. However, they only know how to restrict it from the legal perspective, and do not pay attention to the education of self-restraint, and they cannot eliminate the root causes of competition, deception, hatred, and killing. Moreover, domestic food is strangely expensive, and they do not strive to accumulate it, but instead export it at a low price. Luxury goods are not prohibited. The huge investment in factory equipment is not based on domestic needs, but is used to compete in foreign markets, attracting enemies and jealousy. They also set up military equipment to wait for it. All of this is a self-defeating way. Then they are still unable to stand on a solid foundation. If you want to find a way that can be great and long-lasting, there is no other way than our Confucianism. Why don't those who talk about political economy remove their prejudices and study the experimental theories that have been proven by historical facts with a calm mind?

Big tree. It is swaying on it. Anyone who takes the Jinpu train north and crosses Xiaokazhuang can see it from the east-facing window inside the car. There are three passages in front of the tomb. It used to be the ancestral hall. When the Manchus entered the customs, the family members were afraid of being implicated in the disaster, so they destroyed it. However, the foundation stone still exists, and one can imagine its glory. In front of it are several stone horses and Zhongweng. The wind and rain have eroded it, and most of it is blurred, broken, and broken now.

Luck and Intelligence 253

— Wu Baozhi

A certain wealthy household in Dongshan, Dongting Lake, has an ear disease and is deaf. They run a foreign cloth business. When they were young, they went to Shanghai to do business and worked as a broker. Their monthly income was very meager. They were almost fifty years old, working hard every day. The spring clouds were difficult to unfold, and they only had expectations. They usually had a good reputation. Their friends admired their righteousness, and transactions were decided with a single word. Once, a Western ship imported a large amount of white flannel to Shanghai. A friend was entrusted by a Westerner to sell it quickly, so they asked Mr. So-and-so. They knocked on the door. Mr. So-and-so had not yet gotten up. They hurriedly put on their clothes and came out. Before they could say anything, they had to relieve themselves. They immediately turned into the small patio on the side of the door and urinated. The friend saw that the door was open but Mr. So-and-so did not come out, so they shouted loudly to explain their intention. Mr. So-and-so's sleepy eyes were not clear about what they were saying. The friend only saw them nod, so they hurriedly left. By the time Mr. So-and-so returned to see, the friend had left and closed the door and went back to sleep. The next day, the Empress Dowager died, and the whole country wore mourning clothes. An edict was issued to buy a large amount of white flannel. The official report arrived in Shanghai, and the merchants told each other that the price of flannel had soared a hundredfold. The matter was heard by Mr. So-and-so, who was just complaining about himself. The previous friend came running wildly. Without saying a word, they congratulated him. Mr. So-and-so was stunned and unable to respond. The friend said, "The star of wealth has arrived, why are you pretending to be hypocritical?" Mr. So-and-so was displeased. The friend said, "The large amount of white flannel is all in your hands. Now the market price has soared a hundredfold. Yesterday, one word made you a giant fortune." Mr. So-and-so argued hard and said that they had wrongly visited yesterday morning and that they were still drowsy and that their words had not yet entered their ears, so they had never agreed to their request. The friend was usually sincere and honest, so they told them that the Western merchant was eagerly waiting for a reply. They opened the door and Mr. So-and-so was relieving himself. They spoke and Mr. So-and-so nodded, so they did not wait for the signing procedure and immediately made a deal. By the time the Shanghai Gazette arrived, this was the only batch on the market. Mr. So-and-so suddenly realized. It turned out that what the friend thought was a nod was actually a shiver from the cold. They could not help but be dumbfounded. They then agreed to divide the profits equally. From then on, they ran their own foreign goods store and expanded their years of experience. They had a surplus every year. In less than ten years, their family fortune increased to several million. To this day, their descendants have not declined and have carried on their family. I have a long-standing relationship with Mr. So-and-so, so I know the whole story of their rise. People say that Mr. So-and-so was blessed by Heaven. They are truly a lucky child. I strongly doubt this statement. If Mr. So-and-so did not have an outstanding reputation and sound intelligence, even if they could get this opportunity, it would be in vain. It all depends on their inherent intelligence and reserve. The other day, I watched the Mingxing Company's "Lucky Star" and felt that luck cannot be sought by chance. I remembered the wealthy household Mr. So-and-so and wrote about it to further prove that my views are not wrong.

A Record of Living Together in the Military and at Home (19) 254

— The Master of Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter 10: Powerful People Abuse the Law and Discipline, but Fortunately There Are Women to Comfort Them; People Who Take Shortcuts and Bribe Their Way to Success are Appointed Commanders, but Mountain Bandits are Recruited and Annoyed. Chengqi Officer sneered, "This is even more ridiculous. I don't know how many people have come to see the Commander-in-Chief today. If you all want us to keep asking the superiors, we four or five guys will break our legs and still be too busy. We must ask our Director to submit an official request to the Commander-in-Chief to send twice or three times as many Chengqi officers. Besides, the Commander-in-Chief has a bad temper. If he is annoyed, he will kick us a few times. Who will pay for the medical expenses to treat our injuries?" After saying this, he laughed loudly, then grabbed the name card and walked out angrily, muttering a lot of dirty words. He vaguely heard that he was scolding something and something playful. An Yutian was so angry that he could no longer bear it. He suddenly made up his mind. It doesn't matter if he doesn't see him. He followed the Chengqi officer's back and walked out. Unexpectedly, the Chengqi officer walked to the door and turned his head to scold him again, "You can't leave. I have already submitted the card. If the Commander-in-Chief summons you and I can't find you, how can I dismiss the job? Who asked you to come? Now that you're here, you can't just leave. It's not convenient." An Yutian couldn't leave and didn't want to fight them head-on, so he had to sit back and wait for a result. They wouldn't force him to spend the night here. But after An Yutian gave in, the Chengqi officers became even more arrogant, as if scaring monkeys with chickens, punishing one to warn a hundred, suppressing the dozen or so poor people sitting there, who didn't dare to breathe loudly. They waited until the lights came on and even passed the time when ordinary people had dinner. They clearly heard that Governor Ye had arrived at Xihua Garden to entertain foreign guests. A gust of wind blew over the military music from the banquet. The Chengqi officer stood by the door and issued an order-like statement with his eyes facing the sky, "The Commander-in-Chief has a banquet and can no longer meet guests. Everyone disperse. Those who want to come again, please come early tomorrow." These people were like receiving a special amnesty from the Chief of State, escaping the disaster of this prison. Each with an iron-green face, supporting a numb body, and drooping their heads, they filed out, as if being able to escape alive was already very fortunate. Who would dare to criticize the Chengqi officer's untouchable scales and question him why he didn't speak earlier? An Yutian had just escaped to the door mixed in the crowd when he heard the Chengqi officer scolding his back, "It's cheap for this kid. If the Commander-in-Chief weren't hosting guests tonight, everyone would hear that I would definitely trap this kid until midnight before forgiving him."

South Shanghai: Yesterday, approximately 40 ships arrived from various gangs, with 180 ships stored in the port, totaling around 30,000 shi of cargo. The Changxi gang accounted for the majority. The opening prices of various goods fluctuated by around 0.2 yuan in the morning. Fresh Changkun white japonica rice was slightly loose, with the medium grade falling back by 0.2 yuan. Early and late indica rice and foreign tip rice and Yuan rice all experienced small declines of 0.2-0.3 yuan.

Jiangxi Yuan Rice Continues to Arrive 265

Foreign Rice Has an Outbound Route to Jiangbei

Yesterday's foreign rice sales were still active, and the market remained firm. Mainland gangs continued to purchase rice, and Jiangbei gangs collected and loaded small bags. The local countryside also inquired about prices. The total market volume of small-bag rice was 3,000 bags, priced at 10.047-10.15 yuan. Red small-bag rice was 500 bags, priced at 9.45 yuan. Eggplant-colored brown rice was 700 bags, priced at 9.4 yuan. Annam japonica rice had average demand, with 700 bags sold yesterday. The quality was slightly lower, and the price also fell, opening at 12.5-12.15 yuan.

Jiangxi machine-milled Yuan rice has been very popular in the local market recently. Yesterday, a new batch arrived, with over 1,000 bags purchased by local businesses, priced at 14.7-13.8 yuan, and the lower grade at 13.2-13.3 yuan.

Flour Prices Difficult to Sustain 266

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the quoted prices for foreign wheat fell by around 0.2-0.3 yuan, causing considerable market fatigue. Opening prices were unstable, with July only at 1.87 yuan. However, due to many bullish traders from outside the industry, unfavorable weather conditions, and factories continuing to restrict supply, buyers prevailed, and the market improved. Closing prices were better by around 0.05 yuan. By the afternoon opening, standard flour continued to decline, and actual sales remained as quiet as usual. In this environment, even the desire to maintain prices felt difficult, and as wheat eased, reducing costs, flour prices naturally became difficult to sustain. Therefore, market sentiment was flat and soft, with a general trend towards small declines. As a result, the July contract was down by 0.025 yuan, and the August to November contracts were down by 0.05 yuan.

Main Reasons for the Decline in Listed Wheat 267

Quoted Prices for New Wheat in Production Areas are Easing

Financial Tightening and Sluggish Flour Sales

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market, all months trended towards a weak outlook again. The quoted prices for new wheat in various production areas were unexpectedly easing step by step. For example, the high-quality wheat from Wuxi has reached 5.15 yuan, down another 0.4 yuan from the price quoted a week ago. Other areas such as Danyang, Zhenjiang, and Nanjing also reported declines. It can be seen that financial tightening and sluggish flour sales are the main reasons for the wheat market's decline. The market was therefore very volatile, and July opening prices fell sharply, opening at 3.13 yuan, with August at 3.24 yuan. The unfavorable situation can easily be imagined. By the afternoon opening, transactions were very limited. Because the flour market was able to hold steady, the decline temporarily stopped. As a result, the July contract declined by 0.06 yuan, the August contract by 0.04 yuan, and the September contract by 0.02 yuan. The remaining months were not opened. New wheat continued to be loaded, but the factories were unwilling to offer prices. Three ships of Anting wheat arrived, but no transactions were made.

Metals 270

A Silent Scene in Metals

Metal transactions have been quiet recently because guest merchants are not buying much, and factories have little demand, resulting in a very quiet market. Prices in various markets have generally declined. The main items are listed below:

English Sheet Steel Supply Exceeds Demand: Recent transactions of English sheet steel have been very sluggish. Guest merchants and factories have not used up previous purchases, so there are no buyers. The supply is plentiful, exceeding demand, leading to a very inactive market. Prices are quite low. For example, 2.5-cent sheets are estimated at 8 taels, 2 maces and 5 candareens to 6 taels per dan (unit of weight); 7.5-cent sheets at 5 taels, 7 maces and 5 candareens; and 1-cent sheets at 5 taels and 2 maces. It is said that only sixty or seventy dan were sold on the market yesterday.

Refined Antimony’s Price Continues to Fall: Since foreign firms stopped trading, the market has been exceptionally quiet. There are reportedly large stocks in Shanghai, and prices are still expected to fall. Yesterday's sales were said to be only 185 taels per ton.

Pig Lead: A Strong Exterior, Weak Interior: Recently, overseas prices have been falling, so local prices have followed suit. Yesterday's estimate was 13 taels and 1 mace and 5 candareens, a decrease of 1 mace compared to the previous price. It is said that since help from outside stopped, factory business has been slow. Therefore, the market situation is unlikely to change soon. Although quoted prices are around 13 taels, 3 maces and 4 candareens, actual transactions are rare.

American Galvanized Iron Arriving Continuously: Sales of American galvanized iron have also been sluggish recently. Although prices are gradually decreasing, shipments continue to arrive. Besides inquiries, actual transactions are few. Currently, the market price for 48-gauge sheets is estimated at 15 taels, 38-gauge sheets at 14 taels and 7 maces and 5 candareens, 33-gauge sheets at 13 taels and 5 maces, and 25-gauge sheets at 12 taels and 5 maces.
